I.    Project Implementation and Monitoring
133.  The PFPSAL II will be implemented in accordance with the procedures for adjustment
loans in Turkey established under the first PFPSAL and earlier adjustment operations. The
financial and public sector program is being implemented by the Undersecretariat of Treasury, in
cooperation with the Central Bank of Turkey, the BRSA, the SDIF, the Ministry of Finance, the
State Planning Organization, and the Turkish Court of Accounts. The Bank will conduct regular
supervision of the PFPSAL II in close collaboration with the IMF. To help ensure timely
implementation of the program, the Bank team has confirmed with the Government that each
condition for release of the second and third tranches of PFPSAL II as presented in the policy
matrix has been clearly assigned and is owned by a particular government agency. The high-
level Steering Committee for the PEM component of the public sector reform program is
responsible for ensuring effective cooperation among the numerous ministries and line agencies,
and arrangements will be put in place to ensure effective implementation of the national anti-
corruption strategy. Disbursement arrangements for PFPSAL II will be fully consistent with
Bank practice for adjustment loans. Upon notification by the Bank of loan effectiveness
(immediately following Board approval), the proceeds of the first tranche of the loan (excluding
the front-end fees) will be deposited by the Bank into the designated Deposit Accounts at the
request of the Borrower. In accordance with the Operational Directive on the Simplification of
Disbursement Rules under Structural Adjustment and Sector Adjustment Loans (February 8,
1996), disbursements will not be linked to specific purchases. The closing date for the Loan will
be December 31, 2002.
134.  Monitoring. The Bank will carry out regular supervision of the PFPSAL II program in
close coordination with the IMF. Progress in all areas of the program will be monitored against
agreed benchmarks and the conditions for release of the second and third tranches of the loan. A
daily monitoring system is in place with support from the IMF for key macroeconomic indicators
such as interest rates, the exchange rate, bank deposits and CBT net domestic assets and gross
international reserves. Monthly monitoring is in place for inflation, the fiscal balance and the
external accounts. Quarterly quantitative benchmarks for domestic interest rates, the maturity of
new domestic borrowing and private capital inflows have been established on the basis of the
IMF program. In the financial sector, an upgraded monitoring framework for the banks is being
established as described in the risks section above.  Quantitative benchmarks have been
established for the social expenditure envelopes under the 2002 budget. Benchmarks have also
been set for staffing levels in the civil service and SEEs, and these will be monitored on a
continuous basis, including the extent of staff reductions in the state and SDIF banks. Additional
quantitative benchmarks will be established, if needed, as events unfold on the ground. An
extensive monitoring of the broader social impact of the overall reform program is being carried
out through a combination of activities under the PSSP, ARIP and Social Risk Mitigation
Project.

135. I am satisfied that the proposed loan complies with the Articles of Agreement of the Bank
and I recommend that the Executive Directors approve the loan.

REPUBLIC OF TURKEY
PRIME MINISTRY
The Undersecretariat of Treasury
Ref. B.02.1.HM.0.DEt.01.05.197/17484                      Ankara, March 19, 2002
Mr. James D. Wolfensohn
President
The World Bank
Washington DC 20433
U.S.A.
Dear Mr. Wolfensohn,
1.    Since adopting its strengthened economic program in May, the Government has made
significant progress stabilizing the economy and laying the foundation for sustainable growth
and employment creation in response to the economic crisis which hit Turkey in February 2001.
At the macroeconomic level, we have succeeded in overcoming the initial impact of the crisis on
Turkey's financial markets. Interest rates have fallen to below 70 percent, compared with crisis
peaks of well over 100 percent, and the fiscal program met the target for the primary surplus of
the consolidated public sector of 5.5 percent of GNP in 2001. The floating exchange rate regime
has been successfully introduced and a degree of exchange rate stability achieved following the
large devaluation after February. The exchange rate adjustment has helped shift the current
account to an estimated surplus of US$3.3 billion in 2001, compared to the US$9.8 billion deficit
registered in 2000. The initial spike in prices induced by the devaluation has been contained,
although it is clear that inflationary pressures remain significant. As a result of the crisis and the
need to absorb the costs of bank restructuring, the stock of net public debt to GNP has increased
to an estimated 91 percent of GNP by the end of 2001. In order to ensure debt sustainability and
economic recovery, and resume the disinflation process, we are putting into place further
strengthened policies for 2002 as described below under a new medium-term macroeconomic
framework. Our macroeconomic objectives for 2002 include an increase in the primary surplus
to 6.5 percent of GNP, a reduction in inflation to 35 percent and a fall in nominal interest rates to
the 55 percent range by December 2002, restored GNP growth of 3 percent, and a decline in the
public debt to GNP ratio to about 81 percent.
2.    With regard to our structural program, we have achieved some notable success in
implementing the reforms to the financial and public sectors supported by the programmatic
financial and public sector adjustment loan (PFPSAL) approved by the World Bank in July 2001.
In the banking sector, we have taken further steps to upgrade the regulatory regime, to enhance



the BRSA's institutional capacity, to strengthen the capital base of the private banks and resolve
SDIF banks, and to undertake financial and operational restructuring of the stae n  ba.
In. ceroain areas of the program, notably privatization of Valcif Bank and buldget consolidation,
we1have encbuntered some delays due to market sentiment and ile complexifies of the.reqjirbd
mstnrutional reforms. In other areas, such as banjk recapitalization and replacement of the public
accbuntinglawTh we have expa-nded the prograam.beyond the PFPSAL benchmarrcs and formulated
new measuros which were nol fofeseen in the original program.
3.    Tho Goverunent is also moving ahead with structural reforns to promote private seetor
developmnnt and improve the investment climate including an ac3ori plan to improve the foreign
direct investment (FDI) climate prepared in collaboration with FIAS. As part of this agenda, we
intend to complete the actions required for release of the second tranche of the Econoomic Refonn
Loan (ERL). Our program for paivate sector development includes the following actiond:
 In agricultfre, we have initiated the rollout of the direct income support (DIS) progrpn)at the
national Jevel with slipport from the Agriculture Refqrrm Trnpl4metaton Pro ect Lgslation
liberalizmn the tobacco sector and authorizing the privatizatiorr of TE(EL, which was
originally votoed by the President in July 2001, was enacted on January 9, 2002.
 Inh the energy sector, the new Energy Markets Regulatory Agency (EMRA) has been
-stablishc4d and is now preparing the secondary legislation required to establish energy
'mavets in Turkey. Average electricity sales tariffs for the Turkish Electricity Trade and
Cor#raLting Company, the successor to TEAS, are currently above US 4.5 cents per kwh in
line with the financial recovery plan. Future tariff policy will be datermined by EMRA as
Mnvisagedin the Electricity Markets Law (No. 4628).
 In telecornmunications, an international consulting firm was hired in December 2001 to assist
Turk Te]ekom with the prepration of a plan to complete the corporatization of the compwny.
The new tender comiittee for T3urk Telekaom has been established and wil prepare a new.
privatization plan for the company which is expected to be approved by the Government in
April 2002. Full licensing authority has been transferred to the Teleconirnuniafions
Regulatory Authoiity which is now preparing the required secondary legislation in line *ith
EBT standards.
*  The PA expects to complete the divestiture of 51 percent of BED hM2   (steel) by emd-March
2002 and of TUPRAS (refinery) by end-June 2002, at tbh latest PTivatization of rnedium
and s=all scale comnpanies in the PA's portfolio will also be relaunched in 2W2.
* The FDI action plan was adopted by the Govenment in )ecember 2001. The plan includes
the submission of a new drat FDI law to ?arliament in le with the fmdin&s of the FIAS
study by end-June 2002. The plan also calls for the developrinent of ab investu=t pro0tnoii
strategy which could lead to the establishment of an' investment prom6tiou agency.
Furtherrnore, we will establish an Investor Council consisting of prominent business'
representatives from Turkey and abroad.
4.    In order to move further towards our goal of a competitive electricity market, the
Government has decided on the following process for resolving the pending transfer of opeating
righis (TOOR-) and build-operate-transfer (:BOT) projects on the basis of the Constitutional Court
decision .aumulling parts of provisional artiples No. 4 and 8 of the Blectricity Markets Law. This
pr,qess wiU be adjusted, if needed, on the Vasis of the written Constitutional Court decision
2



expected to be published by end-March 2002, as well as the timing of the High Administration
Court (Danistay) clarification mentioned below and any subsequent Danistay opinions that are
required. License regulations for generation and distribution will be issued by the Energy
Market Regulatory Agency by end-May 2002.
* As soon as the Constitutional Court decision is published, the Government will seek further
clarification from Danistay in order to determine the list of TOOR projects, if any, which are
eligible for Treasury guarantees.
* The sponsors of TOOR generation and distribution projects eligible for Treasury guarantees
will be informed by June 2002 of the amendments required to bring the projects into
conformity with the license regulations issued by EMRA and the Electricity Markets Law.
* With the exception of assets linked to eligible TOOR projects, if any, where the required
amendments are made, by July 2002, the Government will transfer all state-owned thermal
generation and electricity distribution assets under the scope of privatization and launch pre-
qualification tenders for the distribution assets.
* For the remaining eligible TOOR projects, if any, by end-July 2002, the Government will
sign implementation agreements including Treasury-deterrnined guarantee principles where
appropriate and providing a non-renewable period of six months to raise the financing. At
the end of this period, the TOOR contracts which have not reached financial closure will
expire and these assets will be transferred under the scope of privatization by February 2003.
* The Government's policy is not to provide Treasury guarantees for BOT projects not
included in the list of 29 projects identified in 2000.
5.    We have made substantial progress in strengthening social protection for Turkey's
citizens under the PFPSAL program. The outcome for social spending as a share of GNP under
the supplementary budget for 2001 approved in June is in line with the program benchmarks
agreed with the Bank. These benchmarks have been set at a level above the averages for the
1998-2000 period, reflecting the Government's policy decision to fully fund its social priorities
even as overall public spending is reduced. The estimated outcome for total social spending as a
share of GNP in 2001 is 15.5 percent, well above the PFPSAL benchmark of 14.5 percent. The
individual components of social spending on health, education and social protection are all also
in line with their specific benchmarks. The budget for 2002, approved by Parliament in
December, increases total social spending to almost 16 percent of GNP. The 2002 budget
maintains public spending on health and social protection as a share of GNP above the PFPSAL
benchmarks of 3.25 percent and 7.0 percent respectively. Expenditure on social protection in
GNP terms is budgeted to increase relative to 2001 resulting in part from the expansion of the
DIS program to cover all eligible farmers nationwide. The Government has allocated TL 1.9
quadrillion for DIS payments in 2002. Per hectare payments under the DIS program for 2002
will be indexed to the 35 percent targeted inflation rate. Should actual spending requirements for
the DIS program exceed the TL 1.9 quadrillion allocation, the Government will take measures to
meet this additional expenditure while respecting the overall fiscal targets. Expenditure by the
Social Solidarity Fund in 2002 is budgeted to be TL 875 trillion (0.3 percent of GNP), i.e.,
equivalent in GNP terms to the expanded level reached in 2001, with continued support from the
Social Risk Mitigation Project. Public spending on education is budgeted at slightly under 4
percent of GNP in 2002, somewhat below the program benchmark of 4.25 percent of GNP.
However, the Government expects to reallocate additional resources from the budget
3



contingencies to the education budget to cover the cost of additioinal teaahers to be hired over the
course of 2002. As a result, aotual public spending on education is expected to exceed 4 percept
of GNP in 2002. The Government is prepared to take farther measures should actual social
.speading 'flI short the budgeted targets during the dourse of 2002.  The Govemrnent is
* comiitted to allo atng ad equate expenditure envelopes for social programs in the 2003 budget

30.   The program comprises three core pillars each of which has a medium-term dimension.
The first pillar inivolves structural fiscal policies to underpin the fiscal adjustment required for
overcoming the crisis and to ensure that this adjustment is sustainable over the medium term.
The Government has introduced a package of fiscal measures to underpin the increase in the
primary surplus to 6.5 percent of GNP in 2002. In order to sustain the fiscal adjustment, the
Government intends to implement further structural measures on both the revenue and
expenditure sides of the budget. The Government has adopted a medium-term strategy for
improving the tax system encompassing both tax policy reforms to simplify the system and
broaden the tax base and institutional changes to modernize tax administration in line with
international and OECD norms. The Government has initiated a comprehensive program to
adjust staffing levels in the central government and SEEs as envisaged in the PFPSAL
f1ramework. The public employment program complements other reforms to address the
structural roots of Turkey's problems with public expenditure including reforms to the public
pension system, agriculture support policies and the energy sector under the ERL program with
the Bank. The second pillar of our public sector reform program comprises institutional and
policy reforms to improve public expenditure management (PEM) based on the multi-year
Strategic Framework prepared in line with the recommendations of the Public Expenditure and
Institutional Review (PEIR) carried out jointly with the World Bank. As part of this strategy,
key legislation to modernize Turkey's public procurement system was enacted in January 2002.
The third pillar of the public sector reform program involves broad based institutional reforms to
improve the quality of public sector governance. This includes on-going regulatory reforms in
the banking, energy and telecommunications sectors, a systematic approach to combating
corruption, and civil service reform. The Government has adopted a national strategy for
enhancing transparency and good governance in the public sector which will be published by
end-March. To help deepen its public sector reform program and present core elements of the
program to the public, the Government hosted two international conferences in collaboration
with the Bank. The first conference in September 2001 focused on anti-corruption. The second
conferenice, held in December, focused on public expenditure management reform.
31.   The Government intends to establish before the end of April a new structure for
coordinating implementation of the public sector reform program. This new structure will
involve a small group of key ministers acting as a Steering Group with clear coordination and
program implementation responsibilities. Under the new structure, the steering committee for
public expenditure management reform will operate under the authority of this Group. A
committee will also be formed under the Steering Group to support implementation of the
national anti-corruption strategy. The ministerial committee for civil service reform, which has
already been established, will work in close coordination with the new Steering Group.
32.   We request continued support from the World Bank in carrying forward our public sector
reform program. The specifics of the Government's reform program are presented in the text
below under three major headings: (i) Structural Fiscal Policies, (ii) Public Expenditure
Management Reform, and (iii) Public Sector Governance. This text covers actions taken since
thie first PFPSAL was approved in July 2001 and prior to Board presentation of PFPSAL II, as
well as those actions to be taken for the second and third tranches of the loan. It also presents
additional implementation benchmarks expected to be completed by December 2002. These
14

Government plans over the course of 2002 to: (i) implement mechanisms for monitoring
government project guarantees and on-lending operations, (ii) develop a centralized fiscal risk
analysis capability in the new middle office; and (iii) prepare and disclose a Government Fiscal
Risk Statement. The full institutional structure for the new public liability management system,
including all necessary legal changes, should be in place by the end of 2003. The Government
will then be in a position to issue its public liability strategy as an annex to the planned medium-
term expenditure framework.
Public Sector Governance
54.   The Government's actions to improve public sector governance aim to rcduce political
influencc over economic management and upgrade the quality and effectiveness of Turkey's
public sector. This agenda includes the preparation and implementation of a national strategy to
enhance transparency and good governance as well as the launch of a comprehensive civil
service reform. These actions complement and are integrated with the program of structural
liscal reform and PEM reform discussed earlier.
55.   A national strategy to enhance transparency and good governance in the public sector
was adopted by the Government on January 12, 2002. The strategy was prepared by a Steering
Committee under the leadership of the Prime Minister's Inspection Board and including
reprcsentatives from the Treasury, the Ministry of Finance's Financial Crimes Investigation
Board (MASAK), the Ministry of Justice and the Ministry of Interior. The Government Decree
adopting the strategy and the Steering Committee's report under the slogan "A Transparent and
('leoan Tuirkey: Together Hand in Hand" will be published by end-March. The objective of the
strategy is to provide a comprehensive framework for improving governance and reducing
political influence over the economy which establishes clear priorities and benchmarks, and
emipowers and energizes public opinion to fight corruption. The strategy covers five core areas:
public administration, the judicial system, the political system, civil society and the competitive
private sector. It complements on-going regulatory reforms in the energy, telecommunications
and financial sectors, as well as the reforms to the public procurement system and the broader
financial accountability agenda discussed above. The Government is undertaking efforts to
improve public awareness about good governance and is counting on the active involvement of
national NGOs. The International Conference on Good Governance and Combating Corruption
co-sponsored by the Governnent and the Bank in September 2001 provided input on
international experience and best practice to help shape the strategy. The Government is
committed to active implementation of the full national strategy and has set out a series of
implementation benchmarks for 2002 and the medium term as set out in the matrix annexed to
this letter. To coordinate implementation of the strategy, the Government intends to establish
appropriate implementation arrangements by April 2002.
56.   Priorities under the national strategy to enhance transparency and good governance
include:
* Accelerating the completion of ongoing work, within the framework of public administration
reform, for institutional improvement and financial management.
24



*  xmplarnenting amendmncts to the Law on the Contents of a Deolaration of Wealth, B4bery.

INTEGRATED SAFEGUARDS DATA SHEET
Integrated Safeguards Data Sheet
Section I - Basic Information
Date ISDS Prepared: January 17, 2002
A. Basic Project Data (from PDS)
I.A.1. Project Statistics
COUNTRY: Turkey                       PROJECT ID: TU-PE-P070560
PROJECT: PFPSAL II                    TTL: Lalit Raina/James Parks
APPRAISAL DATE: January 14,2002      IBRD AMOUNT ($m): 1,350
BOARD DATE: April, 2002               IDA AMOUNT ($m): -
MANAGING UNIT: ECSPF/ECSPE            SECTOR: FF - Financial Adjustment
LENDING INSTRUMENTS: SSAL             STATUS: Negotiations completed.
I.A.2. Project Objectives (From PDS)
The main objective of the proposed PFPSAL II is to support the next phase of the
Government's financial and public sector reform priorities in response to the February
2001 financial crisis, while continuing to ensure that social programs are adequately
funded. Key priorities include, in the financial sector: (i) overhaul of the regulatory
framework for banking activity; (ii) institutional development of the new Bank
Regulation and Supervision Agency (BRSA); (iii) problem bank/bank failure resolution;
and (iv) state bank restructuring and privatization; and in the public sector: (i) a further
deepening of structural fiscal policies in support of sustainable fiscal adjustment; (ii) a
broadening of the Government's public expenditure management reform program
including concrete improvements to the framework for budget planning and execution,
financial accountability and public liability management; and (iii) implementation of the
governments strategy to strengthen public sector governance including adoption and
implementation of a national anti-corruption strategy and initial steps towards civil
service reform.



Annex IX
Page 2 of 2
I.A.3. Project Description (From PDS)
The proposed Second Programmatic Financial and Public Sector Adjustment Loan
(PFPSAL II) is the second loan in support of the Government's multi-year financial and
public sector reform program. It follows on the first Programmatic Financial and Public
Sector Adjustment Loan of US$1.1 billion approved in July 2001 (US$700 million on
standard IBRD terms and US$400 million on SSAL terms). It is envisaged that the
proposed PFPSAL II will be followed by (i) two Programmatic Financial Sector
Adjustment Loans (PFSAL I and II) of US$500 million each, and (ii) a Programmatic
Public Sector Adjustment Loan (PPSAL) of US$375 million. The latter two sets of
adjustment loans will all be on standard IBRD terms and are tentatively planned for
December 2002 (PFSAL I), January 2003 (PPSAL) and June 2003 (PFSAL II), to
support the implementation of the program.
I.A.4. Project Location: N/A
Bl. Check Environmental Classification A [ ], B [ 1, C [x ], Fl [ ], TBD [ ]
Comments: Increases in fuel taxes under the program should act to promote energy
conservation and the shift away from indirect agricultural subsidies to direct income
support may reduce the use of environmentally harmfulfertilizers. Improvements in
Public Expenditure Management should permit line Ministries, including environment,
to be more focused in their use of resources.
